Attended a wedding over the weekend hosted by one of the club's members

Not to be confused with the Claremont Resort, the golf club is an older establishment with Tudor styled buildings and a beautiful golf course as its back drop

The bar service was excellent under the circumstances of a very warm day for even Oakland standards

Food service for the reception was excellent as well as the salmon and filet mignon were cooked perfectly

A very lovely venue, it is a private members only club< /text>

<review>I have been here for 9 years. Overall ranking is a B. Good, professional staff, always willing to negotiate a good lease with current residents. Before the pandemic, always good with free coffee and, twice a year, parties for everyone.

There are problems with management enforcing their own rules. Their response to speeders is to have you provide the license numbers of the speeding cars. I would be writing down license plate numbers all day long. Too late to stop the person that took out a staircase, next to a curve in the road. Solution: speed bumps.

The latest problem is excessive (and illegal) dumping. I provide license numbers when I see illegal dumping. Sunday night is a popular night for that, so it seems. Management needs to put signs warning of fines, etc., at the entrance to the complex. It would help to remind tenants that it‚Äôs NOT ok to allow family and friends, that don‚Äôt reside here, to use the garbage bins. It would help to send emails to remind residents to get stuff into the bin. Old electronics, furniture, and other over-size articles should go to El Dorado Waste site in Placerville. I am not the only one complaining about this. So, myself and a few other residents have taken it upon ourselves to do the work. After 3 weeks, with items not being disposed of (bookcases, chairs, etc.), tenants took it upon themselves to dismantle the items so they could be put in the bins. We have to walk by the trash bin-area, so it helps to keep that clean. Otherwise, you may as well live in a barn.

Again, a pretty good place, but you can save yourself some money by renting elsewhere, with the amenities and problems not being much different.</review><pictures>None<//pictures><resp>None</resp>< GmapID>

Vineyards is ok. Pet friendly, garages and nice people. However there have been continuous car break-ins and it's not clear what management is doing to help tenants? There were over 12 last night. Some cars with 2 windows broken out. And at least 15 in mid December. Glass everywhere. $500 plus per vehicle to just fix the windows. It appears that thieves use Vineyards as a shopping mall - arrive at night, shine the lights in each car and if they see anything - break the window and ransack the car. They hit many cars so they take their time alarms or no. There are only 3 entrances - it would be easy and inexpensive to at least put a camera at each entrance - to see who comes and goes between 8pm and 5am. Why not? Instead we get a form letter telling us to call the sheriff's office. They just take a report. So it's ok here but park your car in a garage.</Text>

108028621876751195944<//userid>
< gmap_id>
0x80dcef4da58478eb:0x313b2c91ca0719bc< /gmap_id>
<Pics>None<//Pics>< Review>
Third time at Inka Mama's in the cities of Foothill Ranch, San Clemente, and just recently Aliso Viejo.  All three places were excellent (knowledgable, friendly, and professional staff), the decor/ambiance, and finally THE FOOD.  The prices are well worth it.  I know nothing about Peruvian food except through friends and acquaintances -who tell me that this is the real deal.
This is what I typically order:
Appetitzer
-Ceviche: C'mon... It's Peruvian Food.  I typically judge a Peruvian restaurant by its Ceviche, just as I judge a Thai Food Restaurant by its Pad Thai...  It's a fresh marinated fish in a hot chili-lime juice. There are thinly sliced red onions and chopped cilantro. It comes with 2 slices of potatoes and 1 slice of sweet potato.  It is on the spicy side; which has the tendency to open up the appetite for the main dish.$12.95
-Seafood Paiaya... This is my #1 go to!  It is infused fried seasoned rice mixed in with seafood that was sauteed in garlic: baby squid, mussels, fish, and shrimp.  Be warned: This is not on their "To Go" menus and at the Foothill Ranch and San Clemente restaurants it's not on their in house menus.  It's hidden like "animal style" is to In & Out.  Just ask for it, they'll know.  Paiaya Pronounced "Pie-A-yah". Also if you wanna see what it looks like just Google Image it. $15.95
-Macho Fish... Is Pan fried fish fillet that has chopped shrimp and calamari cooked in a spicy garlic and chili sauce.  It's served with rice and potatoes.  They'll offer a brown rice option for those that want to eat cleaner but in Peru it's traditionally served on white rice. $14.95

There it is. Hope this helps.< /Review>

1561431530969<//date>
<rate>5<//rate><Text>Stir Fresh is one of my favorite casual restaurants. It's great for dining in or taking to go. You build your own bowl using the ingredients laid out salad bar-style and take it to the grill to be cooked in front of you. If you're concerned about spices from the person in front of you, you can always ask them to clean it before cooking yours. Just be aware they'll still be cooking 2-3 others at the same time. They clean the grill often and keep it super hot so there isn't a problem with bacteria or anything like that. Honestly, I think my bowl tastes a little better when the grill isn't freshly cleaned. Your meal comes with rice and sesame bread, and you can add on soup or other appetizers. But honestly, you won't need it. One bowl is more than enough for me, so I only recommend getting the all-you-can-eat if you want to make multiple small bowls with different flavors.</Text><Pics>None</Pics><resp>None< /resp>< Gmap_id>

<rate>5< /rate>< review>
Consistently the best Mongolian style restaurant I've found anywhere in the country.

Single serving or all you can eat.  Frozen sliced meats and lots of fresh vegetables.  I find single serving more than adequate.  Noodles can be added to your bowl.  White rice and sesame toast served at the table.  Flavors come from sauces both premixed & make your own.  Key is to use 10+ scoops of liquid, 2 of which should be oil.  ( Oil keeps for from sticking to the grill, liquid hello steam the vegetables.).

Very tasty with lots of opportunities to experiment with flavors & very filling.<//review>

< text>
I grew up across the street from Stir Fresh Mongolian Grill and have loved it ever since I first walked down the bowl prep line. If you like asian noodle dishes, I highly recommend you give this a place a try. If Sergio is still the manager; you will be in good hands. Stir Fresh has an excellent selection of meats, veggies and sauces in which you build your own noodle/rice bowl. You walk down a long island starting with meats to veggies and finally sauces. You then take your bowl up to a large flat cook top in which chefs prepare your meal right in front of you. Every time I go it is a different experience since it is up to me to create the dish and therefore I love to experiment and try different sauces.</text>

<Rate>5< /Rate><Name>Garrett Davis< /Name><response>None</response><Pictures>None< /Pictures><UserId.>110161113453241075868<//UserId.>< text>
The thing to know about Stir Fresh is that the food is as good as you make it. They give you fresh ingredients and a wide array of sauces, with an optional guide on what sauces to choose. The only time I've ever seen people not enjoy their food is if they were inexperienced and didn't follow the guide. Experimentation is great, but not for your first time.

The service is always good, the decor is a bit dated now, but things are always clean. I don't think the food is particularly expensive for what you get, and is as healthy for you as you want to make it.

Damn it, now I'm craving Stir Fresh...< /text>

<date>1542739834156<//date><review>UPDATE 2018-11-18: Brought my parents here.  They met us, and they loved it.  There were six of us and it was around $60.  Excellent price!  Everyone is really friendly and helpful.

ORIGINAL REVIEW:

We recently stumbled upon some Mongolian Wok places in Los Angeles that were much better than the mall Great Khan experience, so we were glad to find a comparable place here in San Diego.  This location is a little far for us, but we figure it will be worth it about once a month to come here.

They offer a one trip plate where you can take your leftover home with you for 11.95 or for 2 dollars more you get unlimited trips, but cannot take your leftovers with you.

Each trip, you are allowed one bowl, and one small bowl for your sauces.  The Mongolian Wok in Los Angeles allows you 2 bowls (as far as I know) and you can put all noodles in one and all meats and vegetables in the other.  These options are not really needed if the line to cook your food remains short.  I only like these options when the line is long, and you just want to do most of your eating in one sitting instead of getting up multiple times.  Probably better for you though if you do get up.

My daughter ordered spaghetti for her meal.  Nice to have other options like these though we would have preferred she ate the same thing we did.
After about 5 minutes the waitress apologized that my daughter's food was taking a little longer.  Then again in 5 minutes she also apologized.  When she did bring it out, she told us it was on the house.  That was very nice of her, and I didn't feel like it took too much longer.

Our food was great, but the fish I tried I did not like.  It tasted very fishy, but maybe because I wasn't really in a fish mood?

Everything was great, and the cooks were so friendly.  Does it matter if the cooks are friendly or not?  Not entirely, but it makes a difference on your experience.

I didn't order any beer, but noticed they serve beer.  Maybe next time!

The only negative, if  I had to come up with one, is the parking lot spaces are so small.  You will see lots of open spots that you could not possibly fit into.<//review>< username>
Robert Rael<//username>

{'time': 1506725404070, 'text': "Jason,  Sorry about your bad experience at Stir Fresh.   Our grill is very large and therefore very difficult to have even temperature across the entire surface.  Therefore the cooks move around to utilize the hotter and then cooler parts of the grill.   We apologize for the unwanted spice in your food.  There is a sign at the start of the buffet line which warns guests of this possibility.  You may ask the cooks to scrape the grill prior to your meals being prepared or have them cooked in a separate wok altogether.  I honestly don't understand your comment of limited choices.  Stir Fresh offers Beef, chicken, pork, lamb, sausage, calamari, white fish, and tofu for proteins.  At least 15 different vegetable offerings which may change seasonally.  9 different sauces, 3 signature sauces, chili and sesame oils.   We are one privately owned restaurant, not a chain like Ghengis Grill.  We do not have several locations that would give us leverage in getting lower prices from vendors.  Therefore we chose the ingredients we offer so that we can keep consistency in quality, price, and availability."}< /Resp>

<userid>108695516230459977325< /userid><name>Kirt Winter< /name><Date>1507674627050< /Date>< rate>
5< /rate>
< text>
Food is quite good, but part of it is on you to pick the right combination of meats, veggies and (liquid) seasonings. If you don't like spicy, then get in front of any friends who do and watch those in front of you. What's on the grill in front of you definitely makes a difference because all the food takes a lap together. Personally, I like spicy but still adjust based on what I think is in front of me.
There are lots of, uh, "packing techniques" for getting two meals out of the "one trip" option (no take out if you choose "all you can eat"). A few of these are using a small bowl to hold the seasonings, packing down the frozen meat with said small bowl, strategically stacking your vegetables (alas, they don't have snowpeas), and using a few noodles on top to hold everything in place.
I struggled with 4 stars vs 5, but ultimately other than the variability, I always enjoy it here.< /text>

I would describe this Mongolian Grill as average and missing any of the bells and whistles the good ones have. The vegetable bar was missing many of the really good things like snow peas and bamboo shoots it had the standard low cost peppers onions and mushrooms and cabbage with a few extras but nothing really amazing. The oils were the bare minimum there were no spices to add there were no eggs that could be cracked in. They had the standard beef pork lamb and chicken with a couple of seafood things but there were no shrimp and no unusual Meats at all. They had an all-you-can-eat option but there were all these rules so it made it difficult. General cleanliness of the restaurant was a bit on the dirty side and needs an update. The guys that were running the Mongolian griddle use an unusual turning method where they pushed everybody's selections around the table for 5 times and kept walking around and around so the sauces from all the different people got mixed up I never saw them scrape the areas once.
